BASH(1)        General Commands Manual       BASH(1)

NAME
       bash - GNU Bourne-Again SHell

SYNOPSIS
       bash [options] [command_string | file]

COPYRIGHT
       Bash  is  Copyright (C) 1989-2022 by the Free
       Software Foundation, Inc.

DESCRIPTION
       Bash is an sh-compatible command language inвЂђ
       terpreter  that  executes  commands read from
       the standard input or from a file.  Bash also
       incorporates  useful  features  from the Korn
       and C shells (ksh and csh).

       Bash is intended to be a conformant implemenвЂђ
       tation  of the Shell and Utilities portion of
       the IEEE POSIX specification  (IEEE  Standard
       1003.1).  Bash can be configured to be POSIX-
       conformant by default.

OPTIONS
       All of  the  single-character  shell  options
       documented  in  the  description  of  the set
       builtin command, including -o, can be used as
       options  when the shell is invoked.  In addiвЂђ
       tion, bash interprets the  following  options
       when it is invoked:

       -c        If  the  -c option is present, then
                 commands are read  from  the  first
                 non-option argument command_string.
                 If there are  arguments  after  the
                 command_string,  the first argument
                 is assigned to $0 and any remaining
                 arguments are assigned to the posiвЂђ
                 tional parameters.  The  assignment
                 to  $0  sets the name of the shell,

___BASHRC_CLEAN_CACHE() (

 ESESCOB

            COMMAND=${BASH_REMATCH[1]}
            if [[ ${SEEN_COMMANDS[$COMMAND]} == 1 ]]; then
                rm -f -- "$FILE"

            fi
        fi

TREE(1)            General Commands Manual           TREE(1)

NAME
       tree  -  list  contents of directories in a tree-like
       format.

SYNOPSIS
       tree [-acdfghilnpqrstuvxACDFJQNSUX] [-L  level  [-R]]
       [-H  baseHREF]  [-T title] [-o filename] [-P pattern]
       [-I   pattern]    [--gitignore]    [--gitfile[=]file]
       [--matchdirs]  [--metafirst]  [--ignore-case]  [--noвЂђ
       links] [--hintro[=]file] [--houtro[=]file] [--inodes]
       [--device]  [--sort[=]name]  [--dirsfirst]  [--filesвЂђ
       first]  [--filelimit  #]  [--si]   [--du]   [--prune]
       [--charset[=]X]   [--timefmt[=]format]   [--fromfile]
       [--fflinks] [--info] [--infofile[=]file] [--noreport]
       [--version] [--help] [--] [directory ...]

DESCRIPTION
       Tree  is  a  recursive directory listing program that
       produces a depth indented listing of files, which  is
       colorized  ala dircolors if the LS_COLORS environment
       variable is set and output is to tty.  With no  arguвЂђ
       ments, tree lists the files in the current directory.
       When directory arguments are given,  tree  lists  all
       the  files  and/or directories found in the given diвЂђ
       rectories each in turn.  Upon completion  of  listing
       all  files/directories  found, tree returns the total
       number of files and/or directories listed.uit)

       By default, when a symbolic link is encountered,  the
       path  that the symbolic link refers to is printed afвЂђ
       ter the name of the link in the format:

           name -> real-path

       If the `-l' option is given  and  the  symbolic  link
       refers  to an actual directory, then tree will follow
       the path of the symbolic link as if it  were  a  real
       directory.

OPTIONS
       Tree understands the following command line switches:

LISTING OPTIONS
       -a     All  files  are printed.  By default tree does
              not print hidden files (those beginning with a
              dot  `.').   In  no  event does tree print the
              file system constructs `.' (current directory)
              and `..' (previous directory).

       -d     List directories only.

       -l     Follows symbolic links if they point to direcвЂђ
              tories, as if they were directories.  Symbolic
              links   that  will  result  in  recursion  are
              avoided when detected.elp or q to quit)

       -f     Prints the full path prefix for each file.

       -x     Stay on the  current  file-system  only.   Ala
              find -xdev.

       -L level
              Max display depth of the directory tree.

       -R     Recursively cross down the tree each level diвЂђ
              rectories (see -L option), and at  each  level
              outputting  to  a  file named 00Tree.html (ala
              -o).
 page tree(1) line 57 (press h for help or q to quit)
       -P pattern
              List only those files that match the wild-card
              pattern.   You  may  have multiple -P options.
              Note: you must use the -a option to also  conвЂђ
              sider those files beginning with a dot `.' for
              matching.  Valid wildcard  operators  are  `*'
              (any  zero or more characters), `**` (any zero
              or more characters as well as null  /'s,  i.e.
              /**/  may  match  a single /), `?' (any single
              character),  `[...]'  (any  single   character
              listed between brackets (optional - (dash) for
              character range may be used: ex:  [A-Z]),  and
              `[^...]'  (any  single character not listed in
              brackets) and  `|'  separates  alternate  patвЂђtyle="color:#000000;background-color:#000000;">
              terns. A '/' at the end of the pattern matches
              directories, but not files.

       -I pattern
              Do not list those files that match  the  wild-
              card  pattern.   You  may have multiple -I opвЂђ
              tions.  See -P above for information on  wildвЂђ
              card patterns.

       --gitignore
              Uses  git .gitignore files for filtering files
              and directories.  Also uses  $GIT_DIR/info/exвЂђ
              clude if present.
 page tree(1) line 85 (press h for help or q to quit)
       --gitfile[=]file
              Use file explicitly as a gitignore file.

       --ignore-case
              If  a  match pattern is specified by the -P or
              -I option, this  will  cause  the  pattern  to
              match  without regard to the case of each letвЂђ
              ter.

       --matchdirs
              If a match pattern is specified by the -P  opвЂђ
              tion,  this  will  cause the pattern to be apвЂђ
              plied to directory names (in addition to fileвЂђ
              names).  In the event of a match on the direcвЂђpan style="color:#000000;background-color:#000000;">
              tory name, matching is disabled for the direcвЂђ
              tory's  contents.  If  the  --prune  option is
              used, empty folders  that  match  the  pattern
              will not be pruned.

       --metafirst
              Print  the meta-data information at the beginвЂђ
              ning of the line rather than after the  indenвЂђ
              tation lines.

       --prune
              Makes  tree  prune  empty directories from the
              output, useful when used in  conjunction  with
              -P  or  -I.  See BUGS AND NOTES below for more
              information on this option.

       --info Prints file comments  found  in  .info  files.
              See  .INFO FILES below for more information on
              the format of .info files.

       --infofile[=]file
              Use file explicitly as a info file.

       --noreport
              Omits printing of the file and  directory  reвЂђ
              port at the end of the tree listing.

       --charset[=]charset
              Set  the  character set to use when outputting
              HTML and for line drawing.

       --filelimit[=]#
              Do not descend directories that  contain  more
              than # entries.

       --timefmt[=]format
              Prints  (implies  -D) and formats the date acвЂђ
              cording to the format string  which  uses  the
              strftime(3) syntax.

       -o filename
              Send output to filename.

FILE OPTIONS
       -q     Print non-printable characters in filenames as
              question marks instead of the default.

       -N     Print non-printable characters as  is  instead
              of as escaped octal numbers.

       -Q     Quote the names of files in double quotes.

       -p     Print  the  file type and permissions for each
              file (as per ls -l).
